## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor / concentration time-evolution ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is a time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard form of kinetic rate laws in chemical reaction engineering. With only (t, A) available, the most common models are autonomous rate laws dA_dt = r(A) or non-autonomous laws dA_dt = r(t, A) capturing time-varying conditions (e.g., deactivation, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when surface/photolimited or saturated catalyst)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order in A)
- Nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Parallel pathways (sum of orders): dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2) (two simultaneous consumption mechanisms)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Constant source + first-order loss (CSTR-like lumping): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production/feeding balanced by first-order removal)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with limiting capacity or inhibitor buildup)
- Reversible first-order with finite pool: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (A ⇌ B with total pool c2 conserved)
- Time-varying rate constant (deactivation/aging): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective first-order rate constant decays over time)
- Induction/activation of catalyst: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps up from 0 to steady value)
- Periodic forcing (light/chopped feed): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (rate modulated periodically in time)
- Inhibition / limited-access rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates with A due to inhibition or site limitation)
- Mixed time+concentration driving: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (empirical non-autonomous power-law kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), the system is time-invariant and trajectories A(t) are determined solely by initial A(0); explicit t suggests changing conditions (temperature drift, catalyst deactivation, external forcing).
- A negative sign with monotone |dA_dt| increasing in A (e.g., -c*A, -c*A**2) indicates pure consumption; any positive term (e.g., +c0) indicates replenishment/production or inflow-like behavior.
- Linearity in A (dA_dt ≈ -c*A + b) implies exponential relaxation toward a steady concentration b/(c) (implemented as -c*(A-c_eq)).
- Higher powers of A (A**2, A**n) produce faster-than-exponential decay at high A and much slower decay as A becomes small; this is typical for higher-order elementary steps or lumped kinetics.
- A factor (c1 - A) together with A (i.e., A*(c1-A)) indicates self-limitation (finite precursor, inhibitor buildup, or autocatalysis with depletion), producing an S-shaped A(t) if net growth is allowed.
- A sum of multiple A-dependent terms (e.g., c0*A + c1*A**2) suggests parallel reaction channels; the dominant pathway can switch as A changes.
- Multiplying the A-dependent rate by exp(-c*t) indicates progressive loss of activity (catalyst deactivation, fouling) or decaying external intensity; multiplying by (1-exp(-c*t)) indicates an induction period.
- Sinusoidal (or other periodic) dependence on t is a signature of externally driven kinetics (light modulation, periodic feed/temperature control) and typically produces oscillations in dA_dt even if A is smooth.
- Rational forms like A/(A+c1) suggest saturation/inhibition or limited-access effects (finite sites/transport limitation), where increasing A eventually stops increasing the magnitude of the rate.

### 1. `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A**c3*c4 + A**c5*c6/(A**c5 + c7) + c8`
Has unavoidable extra structures unless zeroed. You could set the rational term to 0 (c6=0) and c8=0, but remaining terms are \(A\), \(A e^{c2 t}\), and \(A^{c3}\). ### 2. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + A*c4/(c5*t + c6) + c7 + c8/(c5*t + c6)`

- c0 = 0.2331857324
- c1 = -0.3115334933
- c2 = -0.3115334933
- c3 = -0.08476196603

### 18. `sqrt(A)*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6) + c7*exp(A*c8) + c9`
Has \(\sqrt A\) not \(A^{1/3}\), plus sin(A...) and exp(A...) and linear A and constant. You can zero sin/exp/constant/linear terms, but you cannot turn \(\sqrt A\) into \(A^{1/3}\) for all A. Not match.

Extra constant and log term. Set c4=0 and c5=0. Remaining matches GT. Match possible.

### 20. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*exp(A**(1/3)*c6)*exp(c7*t)`

### 21. `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5 + c6*exp(c7*cos(c8*log(c9*Abs(A) + 1)))`
Even if you set c3=0, c6=0, c5=0, you only have \(A\) and \(A e^{c2 t}\). No way to get both \(A^2\) and \(A^{1/3}\). Not match.

### 22. `A**3*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2 + A*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5/(A*c6 + 1) + c7*exp(A*c8) + c9`

### 44. `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A**c3*c4 + A**c5*c6*exp(c7*t) + c8`
